Life of Imam al-Sawi
beginner
5 min
The Life and Teachers of Imam al-Dardir
Biography of Imam al-Dardir: lineage, education, teachers, and character.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly and spiritual lineage of Imam al-Dardir, his key teachers, and his role as a leading scholar in Egypt.

Core Idea
Imam al-Dardir was a towering scholar and spiritual guide whose authority rested on both transmitted and intellectual sciences.

This lesson introduces the biography of Imam al-Dardir, whose works are commented upon by al-Sawi. Understanding his life helps us appreciate his authority and the tradition he represents.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to get an overall sense of al-Dardir's life and achievements.
Pay attention to the titles used: they indicate his high rank in both scholarship and spirituality.
2
Identify his titles and qualities
List the honorifics and personal qualities mentioned. Notice how they combine scholarly, spiritual, and moral dimensions.
Terms like 'Shaykh al-Islam', 'al-qutb', and 'al-‘arif billah' show his multifaceted excellence.
3
Examine his educational journey
Trace his path from memorizing the Qur'an to studying under major shaykhs at al-Azhar. Note how he gave fatwas while his teachers were still alive.
This shows the level of trust and competence he achieved early.
4
Study his teachers in detail
The passage lists his main teachers and additional ones. Focus on al-Hifni (Sufi training) and al-Sa‘idi (fiqh). Reflect on why these two are highlighted.
His affiliation with the Khalwati order is significant for his spiritual legacy.
5
Reflect on his character and leadership
Consider the descriptions of his moral integrity, his role in enjoining good, and his appointment as shaykh of the Malikis and supervisor of endowments.
This shows his practical authority and ethical stature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمة الإمام الدردير

هو الإمام العلامة النحرير، شيخ الإسلام وبركة الأنام، أوحد وقته في العلوم النقلية والفنون العقلية القطب الكبير العارف بالله أبو البركات بن أبي حامد العدوي الأزهري المالكي الشهير بالدردير .
سيرته ومكانته :
ولد الإمام الدردير ببني عدي بالقرب من منفلوط سنة (١١٢٧هـ)، وحفظ القرآن وجوده، وحبب إليه طلب العلم منذ الصغر، فورد الجامع الأزهر، وحضر دروس كبار العلماء والمشايخ وتلقى عنهم وسمع منهم، وأفتى في حياة شيوخه مع كمال الصيانة والزهد والعفة والديانة .
ولما توفي الشيخ علي الصعيدي ؛ عُين الإمام الدردير مفتياً وشيخاً على المالكية، وعين ناظراً على وقف الصعايدة وشيخاً على طائفة الرواق، حتى صار شيخاً على أهل مصر بأسرها حسّاً ومعنى.
وكان الإمام الدردير يأمر بالمعروف وينهى عن المنكر، ويصدع بالحق، ولا تأخذه في الله لومة لائم.
كان سليم الباطن، مهذب النفس كريم الأخلاق، محبباً عند الخاص والعام وله في السعي على الخير آيد بيضاء.
شيوخه:
تتلمذ الإمام الدردير على كبار أهل عصره، وكان جل انتسابه على الشيخين الجليلين :
الإمام العلامة شمس الدين محمد بن سالم الحفني وبه تخرج في طريق القوم، وصار من أكبر خلفائه في الخلوتية، وعنه أخذ، توفي سنة (١١٨١هـ).
والإمام العلامة علي بن أحمد الصعيدي العدوي المالكي، لازمه وانتفع به وبه تفقه توفي سنة (١١٨٩هـ).
ومن مشايخه الذين أخذ عنهم :
العلامة الفقيه المحدث شمس الدین محمد بن محمد الدفري الشافعي (ت ١١٦١هـ).
العلامة الفقيه المحدث أحمد بن مصطفى الصباغ (ت ١١٦٣هـ). العلامة النحوي المقرئ أبو عبد الله محمد بن محمد الحسني المعروف بالبليدي المالكي (ت ١١٧٦هـ).
العلامة الشيخ شهاب الدين أبو العباس أحمد بن عبد المفتاح الملوي الشافعي (ت ١١٨١هـ).
Biography of Imam al-Dardir

He is the imam, the scholar, the ocean (of knowledge), the Shaykh of Islam and the blessing of mankind, the unique one of his time in transmitted sciences and intellectual arts, the great pole, the knower of God, Abu al-Barakat ibn Abi Hamid al-‘Adawi al-Azhari al-Maliki, known as al-Dardir.
His life and status:
Imam al-Dardir was born in Bani ‘Adi near Manfalut in the year (1127 AH). He memorized the Qur’an and perfected its recitation, and the love of seeking knowledge was instilled in him from childhood. So he came to al-Azhar Mosque, attended the lessons of the great scholars and shaykhs, received knowledge from them and heard from them, and gave legal verdicts during the lifetime of his shaykhs, while possessing complete integrity, asceticism, chastity, and piety.
When Shaykh ‘Ali al-Sa‘idi died, Imam al-Dardir was appointed mufti and shaykh of the Malikis, and was appointed supervisor of the endowment of al-Sa‘aida and shaykh of the Riwaq community, until he became shaykh over the people of Egypt entirely, both in form and meaning.
Imam al-Dardir used to enjoin good and forbid evil, speak the truth boldly, and not fear the blame of any blamer in (the cause of) Allah.
He was pure of heart, refined of soul, noble of character, beloved to both the elite and the common people, and he had white hands (i.e., abundant favors) in striving for good.
His shaykhs:
Imam al-Dardir studied under the great scholars of his time, and his main affiliation was with two eminent shaykhs:
The imam, the scholar, Shams al-Din Muhammad ibn Salim al-Hifni — through him he graduated in the path of the people (i.e., Sufism), and he became one of his greatest successors in the Khalwati order, and from him he took (knowledge). He died in the year (1181 AH).
And the imam, the scholar, ‘Ali ibn Ahmad al-Sa‘idi al-‘Adawi al-Maliki — he accompanied him, benefited from him, and through him he gained fiqh. He died in the year (1189 AH).
And among his shaykhs from whom he took (knowledge):
The scholar, the jurist, the muhaddith Shams al-Din Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Dafri al-Shafi‘i (d. 1161 AH).
The scholar, the jurist, the muhaddith Ahmad ibn Mustafa al-Sabbagh (d. 1163 AH). The scholar, the grammarian, the Qur’an reciter Abu ‘Abdullah Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Hasani known as al-Balidi al-Maliki (d. 1176 AH).
The scholar, the shaykh Shihab al-Din Abu al-‘Abbas Ahmad ibn ‘Abd al-Miftah al-Malawi al-Shafi‘i (d. 1181 AH).
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage is a biography (tarjama) of Imam al-Dardir. It begins by giving his full name and honorifics: he is the imam, the scholar, the ocean of knowledge, Shaykh al-Islam, the blessing of mankind, unique in his time in both transmitted and intellectual sciences, a great spiritual pole (qutb), a knower of God. His lineage traces back to al-‘Adawi, and he was an Azhari Maliki known as al-Dardir. The passage then describes his life and status: he was born in Bani ‘Adi near Manfalut in 1127 AH, memorized the Qur’an, perfected its recitation, and loved learning from childhood. He entered al-Azhar, attended the lessons of major scholars, received and heard knowledge from them, and even gave legal verdicts (fatwas) while his shaykhs were still alive, while maintaining complete integrity, asceticism, chastity, and piety. Upon the death of Shaykh ‘Ali al-Sa‘idi, al-Dardir was appointed mufti and shaykh of the Malikis, supervisor of the endowment of al-Sa‘aida, and shaykh of the Riwaq community, eventually becoming the overall shaykh of the people of Egypt in both form and meaning. The passage then highlights his moral character: he enjoined good, forbade evil, spoke the truth fearlessly, and did not fear any blame in Allah’s cause. He was pure-hearted, refined, noble in character, beloved by both elite and commoners, and had abundant good deeds. Next, it lists his shaykhs (teachers). His main affiliation was with two eminent shaykhs: Shams al-Din Muhammad ibn Salim al-Hifni (d. 1181 AH), through whom he graduated in the Sufi path and became one of his greatest successors in the Khalwati order, and ‘Ali ibn Ahmad al-Sa‘idi al-‘Adawi al-Maliki (d. 1189 AH), whom he accompanied, benefited from, and through whom he gained fiqh. Then it lists four additional shaykhs: Shams al-Din Muhammad al-Dafri al-Shafi‘i (d. 1161 AH), Ahmad ibn Mustafa al-Sabbagh (d. 1163 AH), Muhammad al-Balidi al-Maliki (d. 1176 AH), and Shihab al-Din Ahmad al-Malawi al-Shafi‘i (d. 1181 AH). This biography establishes al-Dardir’s scholarly authority and spiritual lineage, which is important because his work is being commented upon by al-Sawi.

Key Terms
الإمام الدردير
شيخ الإسلام
القطب
الخلوتية
الحفني
الصعيدي

Checkpoint
Through which shaykh did Imam al-Dardir graduate in the Sufi path and become a successor in the Khalwati order?
A) Ali al-Sa'idi al-'Adawi
B) Shams al-Din Muhammad al-Hifni
C) Muhammad al-Balidi al-Maliki
D) Ahmad al-Malawi al-Shafi'i

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Dardir's biography shows his profound scholarship, spiritual station, and his central role in the transmission of knowledge and leadership in Egypt.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage says Imam al-Dardir gave legal verdicts (fatwas) while his teachers were still alive. He did not rush to claim authority. Are you willing to wait and serve under guidance before seeking recognition? What position or achievement are you impatient for today, and can you hold back for the sake of adab?
?
Al-Dardir combined transmitted sciences (naqli) and intellectual sciences (aqli). Most of us lean to one side. Which side have you neglected? What specific step will you take this week to strengthen the weaker side of your knowledge?
?
He was 'beloved to both the elite and the common people' (محبباً عند الخاص والعام). Is there someone you struggle to love or be loved by? What inner quality of al-Dardir—like purity of heart or speaking truth fearlessly—do you need to cultivate to bridge that gap?

Life of Imam al-Sawi
beginner
5 min
Imam al-Dardir's Character and Teachers
Describes Imam al-Dardir's character and lists his prominent teachers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the exemplary character of Imam al-Dardir and the scholarly lineage of his main teachers.

Core Idea
Imam al-Dardir combined fearless piety with deep learning from multiple masters.

Before we explore Imam al-Dardir's theological works, we must first meet the man himself. This passage paints a portrait of his moral character and lists the renowned scholars who shaped his education. It shows that his authority rested not only on his writings but on his personal integrity and his connection to a chain of teachers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage fully
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping. Then read the English translation. Notice the flow from character description to teacher enumeration.
The passage has two clear sections: virtues first, then teachers.
2
Identify the two sections
The first part describes al-Dardir's moral character (commanding good, fearing no blame, pure heart). The second part lists his teachers, starting with two main shaykhs and then additional ones.
3
Reflect on the connection
Think about why the author begins with character before listing teachers. The character description establishes al-Dardir's reliability and spiritual rank, while the teachers show his scholarly credentials.
This pattern is common in biographical entries in Islamic texts.

Source Text

وكان الإمام الدردير يأمر بالمعروف وينهى عن المنكر، ويصدع بالحق، ولا تأخذه في الله لومة لائم. كان سليم الباطن، مهذب النفس كريم الأخلاق، محبباً عند الخاص والعام وله في السعي على الخير آيد بيضاء.
شيوخه:
تتلمذ الإمام الدردير على كبار أهل عصره، وكان جل انتسابه على الشيخين الجليلين :
الإمام العلامة شمس الدين محمد بن سالم الحفني وبه تخرج في طريق القوم، وصار من أكبر خلفائه في الخلوتية، وعنه أخذ، توفي سنة (١١٨١هـ).
والإمام العلامة علي بن أحمد الصعيدي العدوي المالكي، لازمه وانتفع به وبه تفقه توفي سنة (١١٨٩هـ).
ومن مشايخه الذين أخذ عنهم :
العلامة الفقيه المحدث شمس الدین محمد بن محمد الدفري الشافعي (ت بعد ١١٦١هـ).
العلامة الفقيه المحدث أحمد بن مصطفى الصباغ (ت١١٦٣هـ).
العلامة النحوي المقرئ أبو عبد الله محمد بن محمد الحسني المعروف بالبليدي المالكي (ت ١١٧٦هـ).
العلامة الشيخ شهاب الدين أبو العباس أحمد بن عبد المفتاح الملوي الشافعي (ت ۱۱۸۱هـ).
Imam al-Dardir commanded good and forbade evil, and he spoke the truth boldly, and in the matter of Allah no blame of a blamer affected him. He was pure of heart, refined of soul, noble of character, beloved by both the elite and the common people, and he had white hands in striving for good. His teachers: Imam al-Dardir studied under the great scholars of his time, and his primary affiliation was with the two eminent shaykhs: the Imam, the scholar Shams al-Din Muhammad ibn Salim al-Hifni – through him he graduated in the path of the people (the Sufi way), and he became one of his greatest successors in the Khalwatiyya, and from him he took; he died in the year 1181 AH. And the Imam, the scholar Ali ibn Ahmad al-Sa'idi al-‘Adawi al-Maliki – he accompanied him and benefited from him and through him he became proficient in jurisprudence; he died in the year 1189 AH. And among his teachers from whom he took: the scholar, the jurist, the hadith specialist Shams al-Din Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Dafri al-Shafi‘i (died after 1161 AH). The scholar, the jurist, the hadith specialist Ahmad ibn Mustafa al-Sabbagh (died 1163 AH). The scholar, the grammarian, the reciter Abu ‘Abdillah Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Hasani known as al-Balidi al-Maliki (died 1176 AH). The scholar, the shaykh Shihab al-Din Abu al-‘Abbas Ahmad ibn ‘Abd al-Muftah al-Mallawi al-Shafi‘i (died 1181 AH).
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to Imam al-Dardir. It first describes his exemplary character: he actively enjoined good and forbade evil, fearlessly spoke the truth, and was unswayed by criticism. He is portrayed as having a pure inner self, refined character, noble ethics, and being beloved by both the elite and the general public, with notable achievements in doing good ('white hands' is a metaphor for praiseworthy deeds). The passage then transitions to his teachers, beginning with the statement that he studied under the great scholars of his era, with his primary allegiance to two shaykhs: Shams al-Din Muhammad ibn Salim al-Hifni (d. 1181 AH), under whom he graduated in the Sufi path and became a major successor in the Khalwati order; and Ali ibn Ahmad al-Sa'idi al-‘Adawi al-Maliki (d. 1189 AH), from whom he gained proficiency in jurisprudence. Additional teachers are listed: Shams al-Din al-Dafri (d. after 1161), Ahmad al-Sabbagh (d. 1163), al-Balidi (d. 1176), and al-Mallawi (d. 1181). The list shows the breadth of his education in hadith, grammar, Quranic recitation, and jurisprudence, indicating his comprehensive scholarly training.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT mentioned as a teacher of Imam al-Dardir?
A) Shams al-Din Muhammad ibn Salim al-Hifni
B) Ali ibn Ahmad al-Sa'idi al-‘Adawi
C) Muhammad ibn ‘Abd al-Wahhab
D) Ahmad ibn Mustafa al-Sabbagh

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Dardir's character of commanding good and forbidding evil, combined with his comprehensive education under prominent scholars, established him as a respected scholar and spiritual guide.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Imam al-Dardir feared no one in commanding good and forbidding evil. When was the last time you stayed silent when you should have spoken? What will you do tomorrow to correct that?
?
He sought knowledge from multiple teachers across disciplines. Do you limit yourself to one source or perspective? What concrete step will you take this week to learn something from an unfamiliar teacher or field?
?
He was beloved by both the elite and the common people. Is there a group of people you struggle to love or be loved by? What one character trait will you work on to become more like him?

Life of Imam al-Sawi

The Students of Imam al-Dardir
Lists the prominent students of Imam al-Dardir with their names and death dates.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the wide scholarly influence of Imam al-Dardir through his prominent students across different madhhabs and regions.

Core Idea
A scholar's legacy lives through his students.

Imam al-Dardir was not only a great scholar in his own right but also a teacher who shaped the next generation. This passage lists eleven of his most notable students, many of whom became leading authorities in their own time. By studying this list, we gain insight into the vast network of Islamic scholarship in the 18th-19th centuries.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of students
Begin by reading the Arabic list and its translation. Notice the titles, full names, and death dates of each student.
The list appears in a continuous paragraph; each name is separated by a new line in the source.
2
Observe diversity in madhhab and region
Scan the list for indications of madhhab (e.g., al-Shafi‘i, al-Maliki) and geographic origin (e.g., al-Azhari, al-Halabi, al-Madani). This shows al-Dardir’s reach across different legal schools and lands.
3
Identify the most famous student
Look for the last name: Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn ‘Arafa al-Dasuqi. He is a well-known commentator on al-Dardir’s works, indicating a direct scholarly transmission.
Al-Dasuqi’s commentary on al-Dardir’s Sharh al-Kharidah is widely studied.
4
Reflect on the concept of scholarly transmission
Consider how this list demonstrates the importance of student-teacher chains (sanad) in preserving and spreading knowledge. These students carried al-Dardir’s legacy forward.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمة الإمام الدردير
تلامذته:
أخذ عن الإمام الدردير أكابر عصره ؛ فمنهم العلامة الشيخ أبو عبد الله محمد بن عبادة بن بري العدوي (ت ١١٩٣هـ).
الإمام العلامة الفقيه موسى البشبيشي الشافعي الأزهري (ت١٢٠٢هـ).
العلامة الشيخ أحمد بن أحمد السماليجي الشافعي (ت١٢٠٣هـ).
العلامة الشيخ برهان الدين إبراهيم بن محمد بن دهمان الحلبي الشافعي (ت١٢٠٥هـ).
العلامة الشيخ أحمد بن رمضان الطرابلسي الأزهري المعروف بالشيخ شامل (ت١٢١٤هـ).
العلامة السيد الشريف أحمد باعلوي جمل الليل المدني (١٢١٦هـ) الإمام العلامة العارف بالله وخليفته من بعده أبو الفلاح صالح بن محمد السباعي (ت١٢٢١هـ).
العلامة الفقيه محمد الخشني الشافعي (ت١٢٢١هـ).
العلامة الشيخ أبو الخيرات مصطفى العقباوي الأزهري المالكي (ت ١٢٢١هـ).
العلامة الشيخ أبو الربيع سليمان بن محمد الفيومي الأزهري المالكي (ت ١٢٢٤هـ).
العلامة المحقق شمس الدين أبو عبد الله محمد بن أحمد بن عرفة الدسوقي الأزهري (ت ١٢٣٠هـ).
Biography of Imam al-Dardir. His students: The great scholars of his time took from Imam al-Dardir; among them: the scholar, the shaykh Abu ‘Abdillah Muhammad ibn ‘Ubadah ibn Barri al-‘Adawi (died 1193 AH). The Imam, the scholar, the jurist Musa al-Bishbishi al-Shafi‘i al-Azhari (died 1202 AH). The scholar, the shaykh Ahmad ibn Ahmad al-Samaliji al-Shafi‘i (died 1203 AH). The scholar, the shaykh Burhan al-Din Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Dahman al-Halabi al-Shafi‘i (died 1205 AH). The scholar, the shaykh Ahmad ibn Ramadan al-Tarabulsi al-Azhari known as al-Shaykh Shamil (died 1214 AH). The scholar, the sayyid al-sharif Ahmad Ba‘alawi Jammal al-Layl al-Madani (died 1216 AH). The Imam, the scholar, the knower of Allah and his successor after him Abu al-Falah Salih ibn Muhammad al-Siba‘i (died 1221 AH). The scholar, the jurist Muhammad al-Khashni al-Shafi‘i (died 1221 AH). The scholar, the shaykh Abu al-Khayrat Mustafa al-‘Uqabawi al-Azhari al-Maliki (died 1221 AH). The scholar, the shaykh Abu al-Rabi‘ Sulayman ibn Muhammad al-Fayyumi al-Azhari al-Maliki (died 1224 AH). The scholar, the verifier Shams al-Din Abu ‘Abdillah Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn ‘Arafa al-Dasuqi al-Azhari (died 1230 AH).
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage provides a list of the students (talamidha) of Imam al-Dardir. It begins with the heading 'Biography of Imam al-Dardir' and then 'His students:', stating that the great scholars of his time studied under him. The list includes eleven names, each with their title, full name, affiliation (including Shafi‘i, Maliki, Azhari), and death date. Notable names include the well-known scholar Muhammad ibn ‘Arafa al-Dasuqi (d. 1230) and the hadith scholar Ahmad ibn Ramadan al-Tarabulsi known as al-Shaykh Shamil. The list reflects the wide influence of Imam al-Dardir across different madhhabs and regions, particularly in Egypt and the Hijaz. The entry for Ahmad Ba‘alawi and Salih al-Siba‘i appears on one line but clearly refers to two distinct individuals, the latter being a Sufi master and successor of al-Dardir.

Key Terms
تلامذته
الإمام الدردير
أكابر عصره

Which student of Imam al-Dardir is known as 'al-Shaykh Shamil'?

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Dardir taught a generation of scholars who spread his knowledge across the Islamic world.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just read a list of scholars who dedicated their lives to seeking knowledge under a great teacher. Their titles like 'al-Allamah' and 'al-Faqih' were earned through years of sacrifice. Look at your own pursuit of knowledge—are you treating it as a casual hobby or as a life-transforming mission? This week, commit to studying one lesson with the intention of embodying it, not just memorizing it. What will that lesson be?
?
These students carried forward their teacher's legacy to new regions and generations. When you learn something from this course, do you feel the weight of responsibility to pass it on? Who in your life would benefit from what you learned today, and what small step will you take to share it with them before the end of the week?

Life of Imam al-Sawi

The Scholarly Works of al-Sawi
A bibliographical list of al-Sawi's authored works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be familiar with the major works of al-Sawi, especially his theological poem al-Kharidat al-Bahiyya.

Core Idea
Al-Sawi's bibliography shows the breadth of his scholarship across theology, Sufism, and law.

Al-Sawi was a prolific scholar whose writings covered Maliki jurisprudence, Sufi ethics, rhetoric, theology, and devotional poetry. This lesson introduces his authored books and epistles as listed in traditional biographies, with special attention to al-Kharidat al-Bahiyya, the theological work that forms the basis of our study.

Guided Path
1
Read the List of Works
Begin by reading the Arabic list of al-Sawi's works along with its translation. Notice the variety of topics and the presence of asterisks before some titles.
The asterisks are a feature of the original manuscript; they do not indicate order of importance.
2
Identify the Main Fields
Group the works by subject: law (Aqrab al-Masalik), Sufism (Tuhfat al-Ikhwan fi Adab), theology (al-Kharidat al-Bahiyya), rhetoric, and devotional epistles.
This shows al-Sawi's multidisciplinary expertise.
3
Focus on al-Kharidat al-Bahiyya
Note that the present text is a commentary on this theological poem. Understanding its place in al-Sawi's corpus helps appreciate its significance.
It is his most famous work in 'ilm al-tawhid.

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography listing the authored works of al-Sawi. It begins with the heading 'مؤلفاته' (his works). The list includes twelve entries, some preceded by an asterisk. The first work, 'Aqrab al-Masalik', is a well-known Maliki fiqh manual. Then follow works on Sufism (Tuhfat al-Ikhwan fi Adab Ahl al-‘Irfan), rhetoric (Tuhfat al-Ikhwan fi al-Bayan), a spiritual journey (Tuhfat al-Sayr), a poem on the beautiful names of God (al-Tawajjuh al-Asna), his famous theological poem and its commentary (al-Kharidat al-Bahiyya wa Sharhuha), and several epistles (rasa’il) on various topics including prayer upon the Prophet, the Prophet's birthday, Sufi litanies, rhetorical figures (isti‘ara), and a commentary on a creedal epistle by Dimirdash. The list shows the breadth of al-Sawi's scholarship across fiqh, theology, Sufism, and Arabic rhetoric.

Imam al-Dardir's biography frames his authoritative commentary.

Before we study the theological content, it's important to know the scholar behind the commentary. Imam al-Dardir was a prominent Azharite scholar whose works span fiqh, hadith, and tawhid. This passage provides a concise biography and lists his major writings, helping us appreciate his scholarly legacy.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography passage

The passage is straightforward; focus on the names of the works.
2
Identify the three categories of works
Some works are commentaries (sharh), some are independent books (like al-Iqd al-Farid), and one is unfinished. Note the diversity of topics: litany, tawhid, fiqh, hadith, and Quranic exegesis.

Imam al-Dardir authored many works and died in 1201 AH.

Translation of Imam al-Dardir
[13]
A commentary on the litany of Shaykh Karim al-Din al-Khalwati.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry listing the works and death of Imam al-Dardir. It begins with the title 'Translation of Imam al-Dardir' followed by a page number [13]. Then it enumerates several of his scholarly works: a commentary on the litany of Shaykh Karim al-Din al-Khalwati, a commentary on the introduction to the poem of tawhid by al-Bakri, a commentary on the issue 'Every prayer that is invalid for the imam is invalid for the follower' (based on al-Bayli's original), an incomplete commentary on al-Shama'il, and a commentary on the epistle of Judge 'Abd Allah Efendi (Tatarzada) concerning Quran 6:158. Then it lists three more works: 'Al-'Iqd al-Farid fi Idah al-Su'al 'an al-Tawhid,' 'Fath al-Qadir fi Ahadith al-Bashir al-Nadhir,' and a collection of chains of shaykhs. Finally, it reports his death: he was ill for days, confined to bed, and died on the sixth of Rabi' al-Awwal 1201 AH. The funeral was held at al-Azhar Mosque with a large crowd, and he was buried in his zawiya. A footnote cites Surah al-An'am verse 185.

Life of Imam al-Sawi

The Biography of Imam al-Sawi
Introduces al-Sawi's name, lineage, and references

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the identity and scholarly lineage of Imam al-Sawi as presented in the biographical introduction to his Hashiyah.

Core Idea
Imam al-Sawi's biography connects him to the Prophet's family and a chain of scholarly transmission.

This lesson introduces you to Imam al-Sawi, the author of the Hashiyah. We will read his full name, understand the significance of his lineage, and learn about the key sources for his biography. The passage is a standard biographical entry that establishes his credentials as a scholar and spiritual guide.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the English translation. Let the rhythm of the biographical introduction come through.
Pay attention to the nisbas (attributive names) in his full name.
2
Identify the components of his name
Notice the different parts of his name: Shihab al-Din, Abu al-'Abbas, Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Sharif, and the series of nisbas. Each nisba indicates a connection (e.g., al-Hanafi, al-Maliki).
Al-Hanafi here refers to Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyya, not the Hanafi school.
3
Understand his lineage connection
The text says his lineage ends at the blessed 'Alid tree. This means he is a descendant of 'Ali ibn Abi Talib through Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyya. This is a point of honor and spiritual authority.
4
Review the biographical references
The footnotes list several books where his biography can be found, and describe the composition of 'Manaqib al-Sawi' by three disciples. This shows the scholarly attention given to his life.
These references are useful for further research.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمة الإمام الصاوي
( ١١٧٥-١٤١هـ)
(1)
اسمه ونسبه:
هو الإمام العلامة، قدوة السالكين، ومربي المريدين؛ شهاب الدين أبو العباس أحمد بن محمد بن محمد بن الشريف الحنفي الحليفي الصاوي المالكي الخلوتي.
ينتهي نسبه للدوحة العلوية المباركة، فالحنفي نسبة لمحمد بن الحنفية، ابن سيدنا علي بن أبي طالب رضي عنه
(۲)
(1) ينظر في ترجمته اليواقيت الثمينة في أعيان مذهب عالم المدينة» (٦٤/١)، «شجرة النور الزكية الترجمة (١٤٤٨)، «جامع كرامات الأولياء» (٥٦٥/١)، «هدية العارفين» (۱۸۵۱) ، معجم المطبوعات (٣٧٦/١) ، كما ينظر كتاب «مناقب الصاوي على الجملة، وهو أجمع ما كتب في ترجمته، وهو من تأليف ثلاثة من تلاميذ الشيخ الإمام الصاوي، وهم الشيخ قاسم بن محمد الششتي المالكي الخلوتي، بدأ به لكن اخترمته المنية ولم يتمه، فتابع العمل فيه أخوه الشيخ أحمد، ومات أيضاً قبل تمامه ثم بعد هذا أتمه الشيخ محمد بن حسين الكتبي، وتولى إخراجه مع زيادات طيبة الفاضل محمد عبد الحليم عبد الحميد وسماه: «مناقب الصاوي أستاذ الشيوخ وعمدة أهل التحقيق والرسوخ».
(۲) انظر سلسلة نسبه في مناقب الصاوي» (ص٥٥).
Translation of Imam al-Sawi
(1175–1241 AH)
(1)
His name and lineage:
He is the Imam, the scholar, the exemplar of the seekers, and the educator of the aspirants; Shihab al-Din Abu al-'Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Sharif al-Hanafi al-Hulayfi al-Sawi al-Maliki al-Khalwati.
His lineage ends at the blessed 'Alid tree, so al-Hanafi is a relative attribution to Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyya, the son of our master 'Ali ibn Abi Talib, may Allah be pleased with him.
(2)
(1) See regarding his biography: al-Yawaqit al-Thamina fi A'yan Madhhab 'Alim al-Madina (1/64), Shajarat al-Nur al-Zakiyya (biography 1448), Jami' Karamat al-Awliya' (1/565), Hadiyat al-'Arifin (1851), Mu'jam al-Matbu'at (1/376), and also see the book 'Manaqib al-Sawi 'ala al-Jumla', which is the most comprehensive work written on his biography. It was authored by three of the disciples of Shaykh Imam al-Sawi: Shaykh Qasim ibn Muhammad al-Shishti al-Maliki al-Khalwati began it but death overtook him and he did not complete it, then his brother Shaykh Ahmad continued the work but also died before finishing it, then after this Shaykh Muhammad ibn Husayn al-Katbi completed it and undertook its publication with valuable additions by al-Fadil Muhammad 'Abd al-Halim 'Abd al-Hamid, and titled it: 'Manaqib al-Sawi Ustadh al-Shuyukh wa 'Umdat Ahl al-Tahqiq wa al-Rusukh'.
(2) See his lineage chain in 'Manaqib al-Sawi' (p. 55).
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for Imam al-Sawi, providing his name, lineage, and references for his biography. It begins with the title 'Translation of Imam al-Sawi' and his birth and death years (1175–1241 AH). Then it gives his full name: Shihab al-Din Abu al-'Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Sharif al-Hanafi al-Hulayfi al-Sawi al-Maliki al-Khalwati. It explains that his lineage traces back to the 'Alid family (descendants of 'Ali ibn Abi Talib), and that the name 'al-Hanafi' refers to Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyya, 'Ali's son. Then there are two footnotes: the first lists several reference works for his biography, including al-Yawaqit al-Thamina, Shajarat al-Nur, Jami' Karamat al-Awliya', Hadiyat al-'Arifin, and Mu'jam al-Matbu'at. It also describes the book 'Manaqib al-Sawi' as the most comprehensive biography, written by three disciples sequentially: Shaykh Qasim ibn Muhammad started it but died, his brother Ahmad continued but also died, and finally Shaykh Muhammad ibn Husayn al-Katbi completed it and published it with additions by Muhammad 'Abd al-Halim 'Abd al-Hamid. The second footnote directs the reader to see his lineage chain in that same book on page 55.

Correction: The dates are exactly his birth and death years, as standard in biographical entries.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Is your primary attachment to the Prophet and his guidance, or to something else that might fade? What would it take for you to feel that your 'lineage' in the next life is defined by your deeds rather than your birth?
?
The disciples of Imam al-Sawi sacrificed their time and even their lives to preserve his legacy—two died before the biography was complete. Whose legacy are you working to preserve? If you were to die today, what would be left unfinished that others would need to complete?
?
Imam al-Sawi is described as 'exemplar of the seekers' and 'educator of the aspirants'. Are you currently seeking knowledge from living scholars? And are you actively guiding even one person in their spiritual journey? If not, what is holding you back from becoming a link in the chain of transmission—whether as a student or a teacher?

Who Was Imam Al-Sawi?
Introduces the full name and lineage of Imam Al-Sawi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the full name and noble lineage of Imam Al-Sawi, including the meaning of each attribution.

Core Idea
Imam Al-Sawi's name traces his scholarly, spiritual, and genealogical heritage.

This passage introduces us to the person behind the commentary: Imam al-Sawi. Before diving into theological arguments, it is essential to know the author's identity and his connection to the Prophet's family. The names and attributions reveal his legal school, Sufi order, and noble lineage.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic name and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the sequence of names and attributions.
2
Identify each part of the name
Break down the name into its components: Shihab al-Din, Abu al-Abbas, Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Sharif, and the attributions al-Hanafi, al-Hulayfi, al-Sawi, al-Maliki, al-Khalwati. Understand the significance of each.
Al-Hanafi does not mean Hanafi school; it indicates lineage from Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyya.
3
Appreciate the noble lineage
Reflect on how the lineage connects Imam al-Sawi to the family of the Prophet through Ali ibn Abi Talib. This underscores the esteem of his heritage.
The 'Alid tree' refers to the descendants of Ali.

اسمه ونسبه:
هو الإمام العلامة، قدوة السالكين، ومربي المريدين؛ شهاب الدين أبو العباس أحمد بن محمد بن محمد بن الشريف الحنفي الحليفي الصاوي المالكي الخلوتي.

His name and lineage: He is the Imam, the scholar, the role model of the seekers, and the nurturer of the disciples; Shihab al-Din Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Sharif al-Hanafi al-Hulayfi al-Sawi al-Maliki al-Khalwati. Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction, specifically presenting the full name and lineage of Imam al-Sawi. It begins by stating his honorific titles: 'Imam,' 'scholar,' 'role model of the seekers,' and 'nurturer of the disciples.' It then gives his complete name: Shihab al-Din Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Sharif. The sequence of names indicates his ancestry. His multiple attributions are explained: 'al-Hanafi' refers to his descent from Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyya, the son of Ali ibn Abi Talib, thereby connecting him to the Prophet's family (the Alid tree). 'al-Hulayfi' likely relates to a place called Dhu al-Hulayfa. 'al-Sawi' refers to his hometown of Sa al-Hajar. 'al-Maliki' indicates his legal school, and 'al-Khalwati' his Sufi order. The passage emphasizes his noble lineage, tracing it back to the Prophet's household through Ali.

Birth and Early Childhood of Imam Al-Sawi
Describes the birth, family, and early education of Imam Al-Sawi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key events and influences in Imam al-Sawi's early life, including his family background, early Quran memorization, and his journey to seek knowledge.

Core Idea
Imam al-Sawi's early life was shaped by piety, early Quran mastery, and unwavering determination to learn.

This passage introduces the early years of Imam al-Sawi, one of the great scholars of the later Islamic tradition. We learn about his birthplace, his pious parents, and the circumstances that led him to become a student at al-Azhar. Pay attention to the humility of his mother and the persistence of the young al-Sawi in pursuing knowledge despite obstacles.

Guided Path
1
Read about his birth and lineage
Start by reading the first paragraph of the passage, which gives his birth year, birthplace, and the origin of his name 'al-Sawi' and 'al-Khalifi'.
Notice that his name connects to both his village and his ancestral home in Arabia.
2
Learn about his parents
Read the description of his father and mother. Note the special spiritual insight of his mother, as shown in her response to his teaching of tawhid.
His mother's reply illustrates an intuitive faith that did not need scholarly expression.
3
Follow his early education and challenges
Trace the events from his father's death through his Quran memorization by age five, and his repeated requests to go to al-Azhar.
Observe his patience and resourcefulness when his brothers initially refused.
4
Understand his determination
Reflect on how he convinced his brothers and finally entered al-Azhar at age twelve (1187 AH).
His journey shows the value of persistence in seeking knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولادته ونشأته:
ولد الإمام الصاوي سنة (١١٧٥هـ) في قرية على شاطئ النيل من إقليم الغربية بمصر تدعى (صاء الحجر)، وإليها نسبته، وقدماء اليونان يسمونها (سايس)، وهي اليوم قريبة من منطقة بسيون وتابعة لها، أما نسبته الخليفي فللميقات المعروف بذي الحليفة، إذ أجداد الإمام كانوا من أهله قبل هجرتهم إلى مصر.
عرف والده بالصلاح والورع وكثرة العبادة والتبتل إلى الله تعالى، بل كان صاحب ولاية شهد له بها من حوله، وأمُّهُ من بنات مشايخ عربان البحيرة من قرية جبارس، كانت عابدة تقية ورعة، روي أن الإمام قرأ عليها شيئاً من علوم التوحيد بنية تعليمها، فقالت له: يا ولدي؛ كل هذا الذي تقرؤه علي وتقوله لي هو في قلبي، غير أني لا أستطيع أن أعبر عنه بعبارات كعباراتك.
نشأ في حجر أبيه في رياض من التقوى والمعرفة، فبدأ بحفظ القرآن بإشاراته ومتابعته، وما لبث أن توفي والده وهو دون الخامسة، وأتم حفظه وهو ابن خمس سنين، ثم تولى إخوته رعايته، فطلب منهم الإذن له بالسفر لطلب العلم في الأزهر بالقاهرة، فمنعوه لصغر سنه يومئذ، فسكن فترةً راضياً، ثم قرَّ منهم إلى قرية القضابة وله فيها بعض من أقاربه فأخبرهم يعزمه على طلب العلم، فأكرموه وأمَّنوه، ثم كان أن اقتنع إخوته بفكرته التي ألح في طلبها، فدخل القاهرة قاصداً الأزهر سنة (١١٨٧هـ) وعمره.
His birth and upbringing: Imam al-Sawi was born in the year 1175 AH in a village on the bank of the Nile in the Gharbiyya province of Egypt called Sa' al-Hajar, and to it is his attribution. The ancient Greeks called it Sais. Today it is near the Basiun region and belongs to it. As for his attribution 'al-Khalifi', it is for the miqat known as Dhu al-Hulayfa, since the ancestors of the Imam were from its people before their migration to Egypt. His father was known for righteousness, piety, abundant worship, and devotion to God Almighty; indeed, he was a possessor of sainthood, attested to by those around him. His mother was from the daughters of the Arab shaykhs of al-Buhayra from the village of Jabaris. She was a devout worshipper, pious, and righteous. It is narrated that the Imam read to her something of the sciences of tawhid with the intention of teaching her, and she said to him: 'O my son, all of this that you read to me and say to me is in my heart, but I cannot express it in expressions like your expressions.' He grew up in the care of his father in meadows of piety and knowledge. He began memorizing the Qur'an with his indications and follow-up, and it was not long before his father died while he was under five, and he completed his memorization when he was five years old. Then his brothers took care of him. He asked them for permission to travel to seek knowledge at al-Azhar in Cairo, but they prevented him due to his young age at that time. So he remained content for a period. Then he went from them to the village of al-Qudaba, where he had some relatives, and informed them of his determination to seek knowledge. They honored him and made him feel secure. Then his brothers became convinced of his idea which he persistently requested, so he entered Cairo heading to al-Azhar in the year 1187 AH, and he was...
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is a biographical narrative detailing the birth and early life of Imam al-Sawi. It begins by stating his birth year (1175 AH) and birthplace: a village called Sa' al-Hajar in Gharbiyya, Egypt, also known historically as Sais. His attribution 'al-Sawi' comes from this village, while 'al-Khalifi' is traced to Dhu al-Hulayfa, a miqat for pilgrimage, indicating his ancestral roots. The text then describes his parents: his father was known for righteousness and sainthood, and his mother was a pious woman from a family of Arab shaykhs. An anecdote illustrates her spiritual state: when al-Sawi tried to teach her tawhid, she responded that the knowledge was already in her heart, but she lacked the ability to articulate it like him. This shows the deep intuitive faith of his mother. His early upbringing: under his father's guidance, he began memorizing the Qur'an, but his father died before he turned five. He completed memorization of the Qur'an at age five. His brothers then raised him. He desired to travel to al-Azhar to study, but his brothers refused due to his young age. He patiently waited, then moved to al-Qudaba where relatives supported his ambition. Eventually, his brothers agreed, and he entered al-Azhar in 1187 AH. The passage ends mid-sentence at 'and he was...' indicating the narrative continues beyond the available page.

Birth and Lineage of Imam al-Sawi
Biographical account of birth, parents, and lineage of Imam al-Sawi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the geographical and familial origins of Imam al-Sawi, including his birthplace, his nisba, and the spiritual qualities of his parents.

Core Idea
Imam al-Sawi's blessed lineage and pious parents shaped his early spiritual foundation.

This lesson opens the biography of Imam al-Sawi by grounding his identity in time and place. Knowing where and into what kind of family he was born helps us appreciate the environment that nurtured his later scholarship. The passage also introduces the spiritual stature of his parents and a remarkable anecdote about his mother's innate knowledge of tawhid.

Guided Path
1
Locate his birthplace and nisba
Read the beginning of the passage to find the year of birth, the village name, its modern location, and the reason for the nisba 'al-Khalifi'.
The village is called 'Sa' al-Hajar' and is also known historically as Sais.
2
Learn about his father's character
Notice the description of his father: righteousness, piety, abundant worship, and recognition as a saint by contemporaries.
3

She already possessed the essence of tawhid in her heart, but not the words to express it.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمة الإمام الصاوي
ولادته ونشأته :
[ 10 ]
ولد الإمام الصاوي سنة (١١٧٥هـ) في قرية على شاطئ النيل من إقليم الغربية بمصر تدعى (صاء الحجر)، وإليها نسبته، وقدماء اليونان يسمونها (سايس)، وهي اليوم قريبة من منطقة بسيون وتابعة لها، أما نسبته الخليفي قللميقات المعروف بذي الحليفة، إذ أجداد الإمام كانوا من أهله قبل هجرتهم إلى مصر.
عرف والده بالصلاح والورع وكثرة العبادة والتبتل إلى الله تعالى، بل كان صاحب ولاية شهد له بها من حوله، وأمُّهُ من بنات مشایخ عربان البحيرة من قرية جبارس، كانت عابدة تقية ،ورعة روي أن الإمام قرأ عليها شيئاً من علوم التوحيد بنيَّة تعليمها، فقالت له: يا ولدي؛ كل هذا الذي تقرؤه عليَّ وتقوله لي هو في قلبي، غير أني لا أستطيع أن أعبر عنه يعيارات كعباراتك
نشأ في حجر أبيه في رياض من التقوى والمعرفة، فبدأ بحفظ القرآن بإشاراته ومتابعته، وما لبث أن توفي والده وهو دون الخامسة، وأتم حفظه وهو ابن خمس سنين، ثم تولى إخوته رعايته، فطلب منهم الإذن له بالسفر لطلب العلم في الأزهر بالقاهرة، فمنعوه لصغر سنه يومئذ، فسكن فترةً راضياً، ثم قرَّ منهم إلى قرية القضابة وله فيها بعض من أقاربه فأخبرهم يعزمه على طلب العلم، فأكرموه ،وأمَّنوه، ثم كان أن اقتنع إخوته بفكرته التي ألح في طلبها، فدخل القاهرة قاصداً الأزهر سنة (۱۱۸۷هـ) وعمره يومها لم يجاوز الثانية عشرة، لينال قدر الله الذي قسمه له وهو يتقلب في أحشاء أمّه .
(۱) مناقب الصاوي (ص ٦٠).
Biography of Imam Al-Sawi. His birth and upbringing: [10] Imam Al-Sawi was born in the year 1175 AH in a village on the bank of the Nile in the Gharbiyya province of Egypt called 'Sa' al-Hajar', to which he is attributed, and the ancient Greeks call it 'Sais', and today it is close to the region of Basyoun and belongs to it. As for his attribution 'al-Khalifi' [related to] the miqat known as Dhu al-Hulayfa, for his ancestors were from its people before their migration to Egypt. His father was known for righteousness, piety, abundant worship, and devotion to Allah Almighty; indeed he was a possessor of sainthood, attested to by those around him. His mother was from the daughters of the shaykhs of the Arab tribes of al-Buhayra from the village of Jabbars; she was a devout, God-fearing, and pious worshipper. It is narrated that the Imam read to her something of the sciences of tawhid with the intention of teaching her, and she said to him: 'O my son, all this that you read to me and say to me is in my heart, but I cannot express it in expressions like yours.' He grew up in the care of his father in gardens of piety and knowledge, and began memorizing the Quran with his guidance and follow-up. But soon his father died while he was under five years old, and he completed his memorization at the age of five. Then his brothers took care of him, and he asked their permission to travel to seek knowledge at al-Azhar in Cairo, but they prevented him due to his young age at that time. So he remained content for a period, then he left them for the village of al-Qaddaba where he had some relatives, and informed them of his determination to seek knowledge. They honored him and made him feel secure. Then his brothers became convinced of his idea which he persistently sought, so he entered Cairo heading to al-Azhar in the year 1187 AH, his age at that day not exceeding twelve years, to attain the decree of Allah which He had apportioned for him while he was turning in the womb of his mother. (1) From 'Manaqib al-Sawi' p. 60.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage provides a biographical account of the birth and early life of Imam al-Sawi. It begins by specifying his birth year (1175 AH) and his birthplace, a village called Sa' al-Hajar in the Gharbiyya province of Egypt, also known historically as Sais. It explains his lineage (nisba) 'al-Khalifi', which traces back to Dhu al-Hulayfa, a miqat (station for ihram) near Medina, indicating that his ancestors came from there before migrating to Egypt. The passage then describes his parents: his father was known for righteousness, piety, and abundant worship, and was considered a saint (wali) by those around him; his mother was a devout and God-fearing woman from a family of shaykhs of the Arab tribes of al-Buhayra. A story illustrates her spiritual state: when Imam al-Sawi tried to teach her some tawhid, she replied that the knowledge was already in her heart, though she could not express it as he did. Imam al-Sawi grew up under his father's guidance and began memorizing the Quran, but his father died before he turned five. He completed the memorization by age five. After his father's death, his brothers took care of him. He asked their permission to travel to Cairo to study at al-Azhar, but they refused due to his young age. He remained patient, then moved to the village of al-Qaddaba where relatives supported his quest for knowledge. Eventually, his brothers agreed, and he entered Cairo heading to al-Azhar in 1187 AH at the age of twelve. The passage concludes with a phrase emphasizing that this was his destined path, decreed by Allah even before his birth.

Imam al-Sawi was born into a spiritually rich family, with a saintly father and a mother who possessed deep, intrinsic knowledge of tawhid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The mother of Imam al-Sawi had tawhid deeply rooted in her heart, yet she could not articulate it. Is the tawhid in your heart present when you struggle to find words for your faith? Examine the gap between what you know in your mind and what you feel in your soul. What would it take to close that gap today?
?
Your parents' righteousness - or lack of it - has shaped your spiritual foundation. Imam al-Sawi's father was a saint and his mother a devout worshipper. How have you honored or neglected the spiritual legacy they gave you? If your parents were not righteous, how can you break that pattern for your own children?
?
The father was recognized as a saint by those around him. If the people who know you best were asked about your closeness to Allah, what would they say? What is one specific change you need to make so that others see the light of faith in your life?

Early Education and Journey to al-Azhar

Learning Objective

Despite early hardship, Imam al-Sawi's determination to seek knowledge led him to al-Azhar at a young age.

This lesson continues the biography of Imam al-Sawi, tracing his early upbringing under his father's care, his father's death before he turned five, his completion of Quran memorization at that age, and his persistent request to study at al-Azhar in Cairo. The passage shows how his brothers initially refused due to his youth, but after a period of patience and a brief move to a relative's village, they eventually allowed him to go. He entered al-Azhar at age twelve, fulfilling what was destined for him.

ترجمة الإمام الصاوي
ولادته ونشأته :
[ 10 ]
ولد الإمام الصاوي سنة (١١٧٥هـ) في قرية على شاطئ النيل من إقليم الغربية بمصر تدعى (صاء الحجر)، وإليها نسبته، وقدماء اليونان يسمونها (سايس)، وهي اليوم قريبة من منطقة بسيون وتابعة لها، أما نسبته الخليفي قللميقات المعروف بذي الحليفة، إذ أجداد الإمام كانوا من أهله قبل هجرتهم إلى مصر.
عرف والده بالصلاح والورع وكثرة العبادة والتبتل إلى الله تعالى، بل كان صاحب ولاية شهد له بها من حوله، وأمُّهُ من بنات مشایخ عربان البحيرة من قرية جبارس، كانت عابدة تقية ،ورعة روي أن الإمام قرأ عليها شيئاً من علوم التوحيد بنيَّة تعليمها، فقالت له: يا ولدي؛ كل هذا الذي تقرؤه عليَّ وتقوله لي هو في قلبي، غير أني لا أستطيع أن أعبر عنه يعيارات كعباراتك
نشأ في حجر أبيه في رياض من التقوى والمعرفة، فبدأ بحفظ القرآن بإشاراته ومتابعته، وما لبث أن توفي والده وهو دون الخامسة، وأتم حفظه وهو ابن خمس سنين، ثم تولى إخوته رعايته، فطلب منهم الإذن له بالسفر لطلب العلم في الأزهر بالقاهرة، فمنعوه لصغر سنه يومئذ، فسكن فترةً راضياً، ثم قرَّ منهم إلى قرية القضابة وله فيها بعض من أقاربه فأخبرهم يعزمه على طلب العلم، فأكرموه ،وأمَّنوه، ثم كان أن اقتنع إخوته بفكرته التي ألح في طلبها، فدخل القاهرة قاصداً الأزهر سنة (۱۱۸۷هـ) وعمره يومها لم يجاوز الثانية عشرة، لينال قدر الله الذي قسمه له وهو يتقلب في أحشاء أمّه .
(۱) مناقب الصاوي (ص ٦٠).
Biography of Imam Al-Sawi. His birth and upbringing: [10] Imam Al-Sawi was born in the year 1175 AH in a village on the bank of the Nile in the Gharbiyya province of Egypt called 'Sa' al-Hajar', to which he is attributed, and the ancient Greeks call it 'Sais', and today it is close to the region of Basyoun and belongs to it. As for his attribution 'al-Khalifi' [related to] the miqat known as Dhu al-Hulayfa, for his ancestors were from its people before their migration to Egypt. His father was known for righteousness, piety, abundant worship, and devotion to Allah Almighty; indeed he was a possessor of sainthood, attested to by those around him. His mother was from the daughters of the shaykhs of the Arab tribes of al-Buhayra from the village of Jabbars; she was a devout, God-fearing, and pious worshipper. It is narrated that the Imam read to her something of the sciences of tawhid with the intention of teaching her, and she said to him: 'O my son, all this that you read to me and say to me is in my heart, but I cannot express it in expressions like yours.' He grew up in the care of his father in gardens of piety and knowledge, and began memorizing the Quran with his guidance and follow-up. But soon his father died while he was under five years old, and he completed his memorization at the age of five. Then his brothers took care of him, and he asked their permission to travel to seek knowledge at al-Azhar in Cairo, but they prevented him due to his young age at that time. So he remained content for a period, then he left them for the village of al-Qaddaba where he had some relatives, and informed them of his determination to seek knowledge. They honored him and made him feel secure. Then his brothers became convinced of his idea which he persistently sought, so he entered Cairo heading to al-Azhar in the year 1187 AH, his age at that day not exceeding twelve years, to attain the decree of Allah which He had apportioned for him while he was turning in the womb of his mother. (1) From 'Manaqib al-Sawi' p. 60.
Source pages p. 16

This passage provides a biographical account of the birth and early life of Imam al-Sawi. The passage then describes his parents: his father was known for righteousness, piety, and abundant worship, and was considered a saint (wali) by those around him; his mother was a devout and God-fearing woman from a family of shaykhs of the Arab tribes of al-Buhayra. A story illustrates her spiritual state: when Imam al-Sawi tried to teach her some tawhid, she replied that the knowledge was already in her heart, though she could not express it as he did. Imam al-Sawi grew up under his father's guidance and began memorizing the Quran, but his father died before he turned five. He completed the memorization by age five. He remained patient, then moved to the village of al-Qaddaba where relatives supported his quest for knowledge. Imam al-Sawi studied under the most prominent scholars, who held him in high esteem.

This passage from the biography of Imam al-Sawi introduces us to his academic environment at al-Azhar. It lists several of his teachers and includes a remarkable anecdote that reveals his early distinction. Reading this helps us appreciate the scholarly lineage behind his later works.

مرحلة الطلب والتأهيل العلمي
كان الأزهر يومها حافلا بأساطين العلماء الأفذاذ، وكان من جملة من تولى وصايته العلامة الشيخ شافع الخفاجي والعلامة الشيخ محمد عبادة العدوي ومنهم العلامة الشيخ أحمد السجاعي صاحب الحواشي المشهورة، وكان من لطيف أخباره معه أنه ذات يوم مرض الشيخ السجاعي، فبعث للطلبة أن يحضروا الدرس في بيته، وكان قد بقي درس من شرح ابن عقيل على الخلاصة، فلما جاؤوه قال لهم : هل فيكم الصاوي؟ فقالوا : لا ، فقال : انتظروا حتى يحضر، وأرسل إليه، فما قُرئ الدرس إلا بحضرته
ومن جملة العلماء الذين نهل منهم الإمام الصاوي شيخه في الحديث والتفسير العلامة الإمام سليمان بن عمر الشهير بالجمل، وهو صاحب الحاشية المشهورة على الجلالين والمسماة بـ«الفتوحات الإلهية»، وكان الشيخ الجمل يحبه ويجله
ومنهم العلامة الذي سارت بآثاره الركائب محمد بن محمد الأمير الكبير السَّنَباوي المالكي، وكان الشيخ الأمير يحبه ويستوصيه بالدعاء، ويشهد له بالصلاح ورُتَبِ المعرفة .
ومنهم أيضاً العلامة محمد بن أحمد بن عرفة الدسوقي المالكي، من صارت حواشيه خاتمة القول في كل فنّ وعلم حشَّى فيه .
ومنهم شيخ الأزهر العلامة عبد الله الشرقاوي، كلُّ هؤلاء كان لهم
The stage of seeking knowledge and academic qualification. Al-Azhar at that time was full of giant scholars of outstanding caliber. Among those who took charge of his guardianship were the scholar Shaykh Shafi' al-Khafaji, the scholar Shaykh Muhammad 'Ubada al-'Adawi, and among them the scholar Shaykh Ahmad al-Sajja'i, author of the famous glosses. Among the pleasant stories about him with him is that one day Shaykh al-Sajja'i fell ill, so he sent for the students to attend the lesson at his house. There remained a lesson from the commentary of Ibn 'Aqil on al-Khulasa. When they came to him, he said to them: 'Is al-Sawi among you?' They said: 'No.' He said: 'Wait until he comes,' and sent for him. The lesson was not read except in his presence. Among the scholars from whom Imam al-Sawi drank deeply was his teacher in hadith and tafsir, the scholar Imam Sulayman ibn 'Umar famously known as al-Jamal, author of the famous gloss on al-Jalalayn titled 'al-Futuhat al-Ilahiyya'. Shaykh al-Jamal loved and honored him. Among them is the scholar whose works were carried by mounts, Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Amir al-Kabir al-Sanabawi al-Maliki. Shaykh al-Amir loved him, would ask him for supplication, and testified to his righteousness and ranks of knowledge. Also among them is the scholar Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn 'Arafa al-Dasuqi al-Maliki, whose glosses became the final word in every art and science in which he wrote glosses. And among them is the shaykh of al-Azhar, the scholar 'Abdullah al-Sharqawi. All of these had [influence?]
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage describes the academic environment and notable teachers of Imam al-Sawi during his studies at al-Azhar. It begins by stating that al-Azhar at that time was filled with outstanding scholars. The first group mentioned are those who directly supervised him: Shaykh Shafi' al-Khafaji, Shaykh Muhammad 'Ubada al-'Adawi, and Shaykh Ahmad al-Sajja'i, known for his famous glosses. An anecdote illustrates the respect al-Sajja'i had for al-Sawi: when al-Sajja'i was ill and teaching from home, he asked if al-Sawi was present; when told he was not, al-Sajja'i insisted on waiting for him before beginning the lesson. This shows al-Sawi's high standing even as a student. Then the passage lists several other teachers: Shaykh Sulayman al-Jamal, a specialist in hadith and tafsir, author of the gloss 'al-Futuhat al-Ilahiyya' on Tafsir al-Jalalayn; Shaykh Muhammad al-Amir al-Kabir al-Sanabawi al-Maliki, whose works were widely circulated (described as 'carried by mounts'), and who loved al-Sawi and asked for his prayers; Shaykh Muhammad al-Dasuqi al-Maliki, whose glosses became authoritative in their fields; and Shaykh 'Abdullah al-Sharqawi, the shaykh of al-Azhar. The passage concludes with 'All of these had [influence?]', but the sentence is cut off due to page end. The overall purpose is to establish the caliber of al-Sawi's teachers, showing that he studied under the leading scholars of his time.

الفتوحات الإلهية

محمد الدسوقي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Imam al-Sawi was an undistinguished student at al-Azhar.
Correction: The anecdote shows that his teacher, Shaykh al-Sajja'i, insisted on waiting for him before starting the lesson, indicating his special status and respect.

Checkpoint

C) He canceled the lesson.
D) He scolded the other students.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Sawi studied under the leading scholars of al-Azhar and was highly regarded by them even as a student.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The teacher al-Sajja'i delayed his lesson for Imam al-Sawi. Is there any teacher you have shown such deference to? If not, what is preventing you from earning that level of respect through your conduct and dedication?
?
Imam al-Sawi's teachers loved him and asked him for supplications. Do you have any scholars in your life who hold you in such high regard? What kind of student behavior inspires that love? How can you change to become more like al-Sawi?
?
This lesson lists seven great teachers from whom al-Sawi learned. How many teachers have you actively sought out to learn from? Are you satisfied with your current circle of knowledge, or do you need to expand it despite the effort?

Al-Azhar at that time was full of great brilliant scholars, and among those who undertook its guardianship were the scholar Shaykh Shafi' al-Khifaji and the scholar Shaykh Muhammad 'Ibada al-'Adawi, and among them the scholar Shaykh Ahmad al-Sajjai, the author of the famous glosses. Commentary
This passage is a biographical section describing Imam al-Sawi's early life and his teachers. It begins with a brief note about his age not exceeding twelve years, indicating his early promise. Then it moves to the stage of his seeking knowledge, describing the environment of al-Azhar and listing several prominent scholars who taught or influenced him. An anecdote shows that his teacher al-Sajjai insisted on his presence before starting a lesson, indicating the teacher's high regard for him. Then it lists his teachers in hadith and tafsir (al-Jamal), fiqh and other sciences (al-Amir al-Sanabawi, al-Dasuqi, al-Sharqawi). The passage ends by noting that despite the esteem of these scholars, none reached the status of his primary shaykh and educator, Ahmad al-Dardir.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that 'لم يجاوز الثانية عشرة' means he was exactly twelve years old.
Correction: The phrase means 'he had not yet passed twelve', i.e., he was eleven or younger.

Al-Dardir: The Beloved Mentor of Al-Sawi and His Scholarly Legacy
Description of al-Dardir's biography and his bond with al-Sawi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the profound bond between al-Sawi and his mentor al-Dardir, and appreciate the scholarly and spiritual stature of al-Dardir as depicted by al-Jabarti.

Core Idea
Al-Dardir was the guiding star in al-Sawi's life, a master of both reason and tradition.

Before diving into the theological arguments of the Hashiya, it is valuable to know the author's own teacher and inspiration. This lesson presents the biography of Shaykh al-Dardir, as recorded by the historian al-Jabarti, highlighting his scholarly achievements, spiritual path, and the extraordinary bond he shared with al-Sawi.

Guided Path

3

Consider the qualities highlighted: mastery of sciences, asceticism, purity of heart, and his role as a successor.

في رحاب الشيخ الدردير
العلامة الدردير كان نجم الهداية في سماء إمامنا الصاوي رحمهما الله، وكانت عُلقة كلِّ منهما بصاحبه تجاوز حدود المألوف، قال العلامة المؤرخ الجبرتي في ترجمة الإمام الدردير لله : (الإمام العالم العلامة، أوحد وقته في الفنون العقلية والنقلية، شيخ أهل الإسلام وبركة الأنام أبو البركات أحمد بن محمد بن أحمد بن أبي حامد العدوي المالكي الأزهري الخلوتي الشهير بالدردير، ولد ببني عدي كما أخبر عن نفسه سنة (١١٢٧هـ) وحفظ القرآن وجوده ، وحُبِّب إليه طلب العلم، فورد الجامع الأزهر وحضر العلماء وسمع الأوَّليَّ عن الشيخ محمد الدقري بشرطه، والحديث على كل من الشيخ أحمد الصباغ وشمس الدين الحفني وبه تخرّج في طريق القوم، وتفقه على الشيخ علي الصعيدي ولازمه في جلّ درسه حتى أنجب وتلقن الذكر وطريق الخلوتية من الشيخ الحفني، وصار من خلفائه، وأفتى في حياة شيوخه، مع كمال الصيانة والزهد والعفة والديانة، وحضر بعض دروس الشيخين الملوي والجوهري وغيرهما، ولكن جل اعتماده وانتسابه على الشيخين الحفني والصعيدي وكان سليم الباطن مهذب النفس ، كريم الأخلاق) (۱) .
(۱) عجائب الآثار (۳۳/۲) .
In the presence of Shaykh al-Dardir. Al-Dardir was the star of guidance in the sky of our Imam al-Sawi, may God have mercy on them both. The bond of each of them with his companion surpassed the limits of the ordinary. The historian scholar al-Jabarti said in the biography of Imam al-Dardir: 'The imam, the scholar, the brilliant, unique of his time in the intellectual and transmitted sciences, the shaykh of the people of Islam and the blessing of mankind, Abu al-Barakat Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Abi Hamid al-'Adawi al-Maliki al-Azhari al-Khalwati, known as al-Dardir. He was born in Bani 'Adi as he informed about himself in the year 1127 AH. He memorized the Quran and recited it properly. The pursuit of knowledge was made beloved to him. He went to al-Azhar and attended the scholars. He heard the early [lessons?] from Shaykh Muhammad al-Daqri with his condition, and hadith from both Shaykh Ahmad al-Sabbagh and Shams al-Din al-Hifni, and through him he graduated in the path of the people [i.e., Sufis]. He studied fiqh with Shaykh 'Ali al-Sa'idi and kept his company in most of his lessons until he succeeded. He received the dhikr and the way of the Khalwatiyya from Shaykh al-Hifni, and became one of his successors. He issued fatwas during the lifetime of his shaykhs, with complete integrity, asceticism, chastity, and religiosity. He attended some lessons of the two shaykhs al-Mallawi and al-Jawhari and others, but his main reliance and affiliation was on the two shaykhs al-Hifni and al-Sa'idi. He was pure of heart, refined of soul, noble of character.' (1) (1) 'Aja'ib al-Athar (2/33).

Commentary
This passage focuses on the special relationship between Imam al-Sawi and Shaykh al-Dardir, then provides a formal biography of al-Dardir quoted from the historian al-Jabarti. It first describes al-Dardir as the 'star of guidance' for al-Sawi and notes that their bond was extraordinary. Then it presents al-Jabarti's laudatory biography, which details al-Dardir's lineage, birth, education, teachers, spiritual path (Khalwatiyya), and his virtues. The biography emphasizes his mastery of both intellectual and transmitted sciences, his Sufi affiliation, and his high character. The footnote cites al-Jabarti's work 'Aja'ib al-Athar'.

The Scholarly Stature of Ahmad al-Dardir
Biographical sketch of Ahmad al-Dardir, highlighting his education, teachers, and spiritual path.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly and spiritual stature of Shaykh Ahmad al-Dardir, as described by his student al-Sawi and the historian al-Jabarti.

Core Idea
Ahmad al-Dardir was a master of both rational and transmitted sciences, and a spiritual guide of the Khalwati order.

This passage introduces us to one of the most influential teachers of Imam al-Sawi: Shaykh Ahmad al-Dardir. Through the words of al-Jabarti, we learn of his comprehensive education, his teachers, and his spiritual path. Understanding al-Dardir's background helps us appreciate the profound bond that formed between him and al-Sawi.

Al-Dardir studied hadith, fiqh, and the Khalwati path.

(۱) مناقب الصاوي ( ص ٦٤) .
Translation of Imam al-Sawi: He had a share with Imam al-Sawi, but they (i.e., his shaykhs) held a place in his heart like that of his shaykh and educator, the unique one of his time, the ocean of knowledge, Shaykh Ahmad al-Dardir—may Allah be pleased with him and with them all. In the precincts of Shaykh al-Dardir. Al-‛Allāmah al-Dardir was the star of guidance in the sky of our Imam al-Sawi—may Allah have mercy on them both. The bond between each of them and his companion exceeded the usual limits. Al-‛Allāmah al-Mu’arrikh al-Jabartī said in his biography of Imam al-Dardir—may Allah be pleased with him: “The Imam, the scholar, the unique one of his time in the rational and transmitted sciences, the shaykh of the people of Islam and the blessing of mankind, Abu al-Barakāt Aḥmad ibn Muḥammad ibn Aḥmad ibn Abī Ḥāmid al-‛Adawī al-Mālikī al-Azharī al-Khalwatī, known as al-Dardir. He was born in Banī ‛Adī, as he himself reported, in the year 1127 AH. He memorized the Qur’an and recited it with tajwīd, and love for seeking knowledge was instilled in him. He came to al-Azhar Mosque and attended the scholars. He heard al-Awwalī from Shaykh Muḥammad al-Duqarī with its conditions, and hadith from both Shaykh Aḥmad al-Ṣabbāgh and Shams al-Dīn al-Ḥifnī—and under the latter he graduated in the path of the people (i.e., the Sufis). He studied fiqh under Shaykh ‛Alī al-Ṣa‛īdī and accompanied him in most of his lessons until he became proficient and produced outstanding students. He received the dhikr and the way of the Khalwatiyya from Shaykh al-Ḥifnī and became one of his successors. He issued fatwas during the lifetime of his shaykhs, with complete integrity, asceticism, chastity, and piety. He attended some lessons of the two shaykhs al-Mallawī and al-Jawharī and others, but his main reliance and affiliation was on the two shaykhs al-Ḥifnī and al-Ṣa‛īdī. He was pure-hearted, refined in soul, and noble in character.” (1) (1) ‛Ajā’ib al-Āthār (2/33). And the works of al-‛Allāmah al-Dardir hold a lofty status among the later books of the Malikī masters. His al-Kharīdah, his Ṣalawāt, and his Tuḥfah are never absent from the library of diligent students. So when and how did al-Sawi come to know the guide of his heart to his Lord? In the year when the young al-Sawi arrived in Cairo heading for al-Azhar (1187 AH), after six months he had spent there, his noble, radiant countenance, possessing divine lights, attracted him to Shaykh al-Dardir in order to be included in the circle of sainthood. The two Aḥmads’ eyes fell upon each other, and the confusion of shyness and fear seethed in the young man’s heart, so that a humble, hopeful look appeared, mingled with a compassionate, paternal, glowing gaze whose brilliance moved across the pages of the arriving divine bequest. And Shaykh al-Dardir pledged allegiance to his spiritual son al-Sawi, and accepted him as a lion in the path of the Khalwatī masters—the path of knowledge, action, sainthood, and good manners with Allah Almighty and with His Messenger the Chosen One—upon him be the prayers and peace of Allah. And you should know that Shaykh al-Dardir took charge and wove al-Sawi into a new fabric that time does not wear out. So he learned from him the rational and transmitted sciences—while he was at that time the leading imam of all Egypt in both—and he studied fiqh under his guidance until it reached the point that when Shaykh al-Dardir saw al-Sawi’s handwriting on some fatwa, he would hasten to endorse it, knowing his piety and scholarly investigation. Al-Sawi was constant in attending the shaykh’s gatherings and regularly performing his litanies, never slackening or finding excuses. And al-Sawi held the foremost place in the shaykh’s heart. (1) (1) Manāqib al-Ṣāwī (p. 64).
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This is a biographical passage from the book's introduction, describing the relationship between Imam al-Sawi and his shaykh, Ahmad al-Dardir. It begins by stating that despite al-Sawi having many teachers, none held the place in his heart that al-Dardir did. The author then provides a detailed biography of al-Dardir, quoting the historian al-Jabarti. Al-Jabarti's biography lists al-Dardir's full name and lineage, his birth year (1127 AH), his early education—memorizing the Quran, studying with various shaykhs at al-Azhar—and his specialization in both rational and transmitted sciences. It highlights his teachers: al-Duqari for al-Awwali, al-Sabbagh and al-Hifni for hadith, and al-Sa'idi for fiqh. He also received the Khalwati order from al-Hifni and became a successor. The passage notes his virtues: issuing fatwas while his shaykhs were alive, his asceticism, chastity, and piety. After the quote, the author remarks on the high status of al-Dardir's works among Malikis. The narrative then shifts to how al-Sawi met al-Dardir: al-Sawi came to Cairo in 1187 AH, and after six months, he was drawn to al-Dardir. Their meeting is described poetically: eyes met, and al-Dardir accepted al-Sawi as a spiritual son, initiating him into the Khalwati path. The passage concludes by noting that al-Dardir taught al-Sawi both rational and transmitted sciences, so much so that al-Dardir would immediately endorse al-Sawi's fatwas due to his trust in his piety and scholarship. Al-Sawi was diligent in attending al-Dardir's gatherings and litanies, and he held the highest place in al-Dardir's heart.

Key Terms
الشيخ الدردير
الفنون العقلية والنقلية
الخلوتية
الجامع الأزهر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that al-Sawi's teachers were many and that he had no single spiritual guide.
Correction: The passage emphasizes that al-Dardir held an exceptional place in al-Sawi's heart, akin to a father and educator.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Al-Dardir combined deep scholarship with spiritual purification. Are you neglecting your soul while pursuing knowledge, or neglecting knowledge while focusing on spirituality? Which imbalance are you guilty of, and what change will you make today?
?
He issued fatwas while his shaykhs were alive, showing humility and readiness. Are you waiting for someone else to take responsibility, or are you stepping forward to serve, even if you feel unqualified? What small act of service can you offer this week without waiting for permission?

The First Meeting: al-Sawi and al-Dardir
Narrative of al-Sawi's arrival in Cairo and his spiritual connection with al-Dardir.

The meeting between al-Sawi and al-Dardir was a divinely guided spiritual encounter.

After learning about al-Dardir's stature, we now witness the providential meeting between the young al-Sawi and his future shaykh. This passage describes the moment their eyes met and the spiritual bond that was forged, leading to al-Sawi's initiation into the Khalwati path and his subsequent scholarly partnership with al-Dardir.

Guided Path
