Grammatical Analysis of the Author's Title and the Function of 'Rājī'
Al-Sawi explains the grammatical status of 'raji' and the author's famous title 'al-Dardir'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the grammatical status of 'راجي' in the author's self-introduction and the significance of the nickname 'الدردير'.

Core Idea
Grammatical precision reveals the author's hope in Allah's mercy.

In this passage, the commentator al-Ṣāwī delves into the grammar of the author's own introduction. He clarifies why 'راجي' (hoping) is placed before its qualified noun and the meaning behind the famous nickname 'الدردير'. This lesson unpacks the grammatical rules and the scholarly tradition of self-identification.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the English translation to grasp the overall meaning.
Notice the technical grammatical terms like 'عطف بيان' and 'عطف نسق'.
2
Identify the two grammatical opinions
Find the two opinions about the grammatical relationship: 'عطف بيان' (explicative apposition) and 'عطف نسق' (coordinating apposition). Note which one is considered weak and why.
The weak opinion treats the particle as a conjunction.
3
Understand the nickname 'الدردير'
Look at the explanation of the nickname: its voweling (فتحة on first د, كسرة on second, ساكن راء) and that it applies to all descendants of the grandfather.
This shows the lineage of the author.
4
Analyze the syntax of 'راجي'
Notice that 'راجي' is the subject of 'يقول' and the phrase is either a substitute or explicative apposition. Understand the wisdom of placing it before the qualified noun: to emphasize hope in Allah's mercy, supported by a hadith.
The hadith is a proof for the priority of hope.
5
Reflect on the tradition of naming
Consider why authors mention their names at the beginning of books: to make the book desirable and trustworthy, as an unknown author's book is not trusted.
This is a common practice among scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عطف بيان وقيل : عطف نسق، بناء على أنَّها من حروف العطف، وهو قول ضعيف.
(المشهور) أي الذي اشتهر (بـ) لقب جَدِّه (الدَّردير) بفتح الدال الأولى وكسر الثانية بينهما راء ساكنة وكذا اشتهر أولاد الجدِّ كلهـم بهذا اللقب.
قوله : (عطف بيان) أي: لأنَّ نعت المعرفة إذا تقدم عليها يعرب بحسب العوامل، فلذا أعرب (راجي) فاعل (يقول) وتعرب هي منه بدلاً أو عطف بیان وحكمة تقديم ! على المنعوت الاعتناء برجاء رحمة الله، ففي الحديث: «إنَّ عافيتك أوسعُ لي، ورحمتك أرجـى عـنـدي مـن عملي» (١)، وإنما ذكر اسمه على عادة جمهور المؤلفين من تسميتهم أنفسهم أوائل كتبهم؛ ليرغب الطَّالب في الكتاب؛ لأنَّ الكتاب المجهول لصاحبه غير مرغوب فيه ولا موثوق به.
It is an explicative apposition (ʿaṭf bayān), and it is said: it is a coordinating apposition (ʿaṭf nasaq), based on the fact that it is among the particles of conjunction, and that is a weak opinion. (Al-mashhūr) i.e., the one who became famous by the nickname of his grandfather (al-Dardīr) with a fatḥa on the first dāl and a kasra on the second, with a sākin rā between them, and likewise all the grandchildren became famous by this nickname. His statement: (ʿaṭf bayān) i.e., because when a qualifier of a definite noun precedes it, it is inflected according to the factors, so (rājī) is made the subject of (yaqūlu) and it (the phrase) is made from it as a substitute or explicative apposition, and the wisdom of presenting it before the qualified is to care for hoping for the mercy of God, for in the ḥadīth: 'Indeed, Your well-being is more spacious for me, and Your mercy is more hopeful to me than my deed.' And he only mentioned his name following the habit of the majority of authors who name themselves at the beginnings of their books, so that the student may desire the book, for a book whose author is unknown is neither desirable nor trustworthy.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is a grammatical and explanatory commentary on the author's self-introduction. It begins by analyzing the phrase 'عطف بيان' (explicative apposition) and notes an alternative opinion that it could be 'عطف نسق' (coordinating apposition), but labels that opinion weak because it would require treating the particle as a conjunction. Then it explains the nickname 'الدردير' (al-Dardīr) and its voweling. The main point is the grammatical analysis of the word 'راجي' (hoping) in the author's phrase 'راجي عفو ربه' (hoping for his Lord's forgiveness). Since 'راجي' is a qualifier that precedes the qualified noun, it is inflected according to the governing factors, here as the subject of the verb 'يقول' (he says). The entire phrase is either a substitute (بدل) or an explicative apposition. The author then explains the wisdom of placing 'راجي' before the qualified noun: it emphasizes the hope for God's mercy, citing a ḥadīth that highlights the priority of hope. Finally, the author mentions his own name following the tradition of scholars, to make the book desirable and trustworthy by identifying its author.

Key Terms
عطف بيان
عطف نسق
الدردير
راجي
بدل
منعوت

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The grammatical analysis is arbitrary and has no significance.
Correction: The analysis follows precise rules of Arabic grammar and serves to highlight the author's hope in Allah's mercy, as demonstrated by the hadith and the tradition of scholarly naming.

Checkpoint
What is the purpose of mentioning the author's name at the beginning of the book according to this passage?
A) To praise the author
B) To make the book desirable and trustworthy
C) To show grammatical expertise
D) To follow the sunna

Key Takeaway
The placement of 'راجي' before its qualified noun emphasizes the author's hope in Allah's mercy and is grammatically justified as a substitute or explicative apposition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you introduce yourself, do you lead with your hope in Allah's mercy or with your accomplishments? What does that order reveal about your heart's true reliance?
?
The author placed 'راجي' before his name to emphasize hope over deeds. In one specific area of your life today, can you intentionally prioritize hoping for Allah's mercy rather than your own efforts?
?
You will be known by what you put forward. If your life were a book title, what word would come first—your hope in Allah or your earthly identity? Which word do you want to define you on the Day of Judgment?

The Kunya, Title, and Name of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq
Al-Sawi gives the kunya, laqab, and name of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq and includes all Companions in blessings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between the kunya, laqab, and name of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq and how the blessings extend to all Companions.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr's kunya, laqab, and name each carry distinct honorific meanings.

This brief passage clarifies the identity of the Companion honored as 'the companion in the cave'. Al-Sawi provides three key identifiers for Abu Bakr al-Siddiq: his patronymic nickname (kunya), his honorific title (laqab), and his personal name. He also affirms that the blessings recited earlier include all the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once and then its English translation. Let the concise wording sink in before interpreting.
Notice the three parts separated by commas.
2
Identify the three identifiers
Find the kunya (Abu Bakr), the laqab (al-Siddiq), and the personal name (Abdullah). Understand the technical term for each.
In Islamic naming, kunya often starts with 'Abu' or 'Umm', while laqab is an honorific epithet.
3
Reflect on the inclusion of all Companions
The phrase 'وعن سائر الصحابة' extends the blessings to all Companions. Consider why Abu Bakr is singled out here.
This reflects his special status as the greatest Companion after the Prophet.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أبو بكر) كنيته ، والصِّدِّيق لقبه، واسمه عبد الله الله وعن سائر الصحابة .
His saying: (Abu Bakr) is his kunya, and al-Siddiq is his honorific title, and his name is Abdullah, and from all the Companions.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is a brief biographical note on Abu Bakr. The author explains that 'Abu Bakr' is the kunya (patronymic nickname) of the Companion, 'al-Siddiq' is his laqab (honorific title), and his actual name is 'Abdullah'. This identification occurs in the context of the earlier discussion about 'the companion in the cave' (rafīquhu fī al-ghār), which refers specifically to Abu Bakr. The phrase 'وعن سائر الصحابة' indicates that the prayer and salutation mentioned earlier (in the previous line) extends to all the Companions, not just Abu Bakr. This is a standard doxological formula affirming the honor of the Companions collectively, with special mention of Abu Bakr due to his distinction.

Key Terms
أبو بكر
الصِّدِّيق
كنية
لقب
صحابة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may confuse the kunya or laqab as the actual name.
Correction: The passage clarifies that Abu Bakr is the kunya (patronymic), al-Siddiq is the honorary title (laqab), and his personal name is Abdullah.

Checkpoint
What is the name, kunya, and laqab of the companion mentioned as 'rafīquhu fī al-ghār'?
A) Name: Abdullah, Kunya: Abu Bakr, Laqab: al-Siddiq.
B) Name: al-Siddiq, Kunya: Abu Bakr, Laqab: Abdullah.
C) Name: Abu Bakr, Kunya: al-Siddiq, Laqab: Abdullah.
D) Name: Abdullah, Kunya: al-Siddiq, Laqab: Abu Bakr.

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr al-Siddiq's full identification includes the kunya 'Abu Bakr', the laqab 'al-Siddiq', and the name 'Abdullah', and the blessings encompass all Companions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you call upon blessings for the Prophet, do you intentionally include all the Companions as the tradition teaches? What would need to change in your habit to make this a consistent practice?
?
Abu Bakr's given name is 'Abdullah' (Servant of Allah), yet he is known by his kunya and title. In your own life, what names or titles do you prioritize? Do they reflect your true identity as a servant of Allah?
?
The title 'al-Siddiq' was earned through unwavering truthfulness. In what specific situation today will you commit to being absolutely truthful, even if it is difficult?
